StreamsBuilder {\n    66→\n    67→    /** The actual topology that is constructed by this StreamsBuilder. */\n    68→    protected final Topology topology;\n    69→\n    70→    /** The topology's   public StreamsBuilder() {\n    76→        topology = new Topology();\n    77→        internalTopologyBuilder = topology.internalTopologyBuilder;\n    78→        internalStreamsBuilder = new cannot be {@code null}\n   132→     * @param consumed      the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters\n   133→     * @return a {@link KStream} for the specified topic\n   134→     */\n   135→    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final String topic,\n   136→                                                    final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n   137→        return stream(Collections.singleton(topic), consumed);\n   138→    }\n   139→\n   140→    /**\n   141→     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topics.\n   142→     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, default {@link TimestampExtractor}, and default key and value\n   143→     * deserializers as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n   144→     * <p>\n   145→     * If multiple topics are specified there is no ordering guarantee for records from different topics.\n   146→     * <p>\n   147→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   148→     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n   149→     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n   150→     *\n   151→     * @param topics the topic names; This also means that the work\n   188→     * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n   189→     * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n   190→     * <p>\n   191→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   192→     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n   193→     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n   194→     *\n   195→     * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n   196→     * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n   197→     */\n   198→    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n   199→        return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n   200→    }\n   201→\n   202→    /**\n   203→     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n   204→     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n   205→     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n   206→     * <p>\n   207→     * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n   208→     * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. This also means that the work\n   209→     * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n   210→     * count of any matching topic * @param topicPattern  the pattern to match for topic names\n   217→     * @param consumed      the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters\n   218→     * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n   219→     */\n   220→    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern,\n   221→                                                    final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n   222→        Objects.requireNonNull(topicPattern, \"topicPattern can't be null\");\n   223→        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n   224→        return internalStreamsBuilder.stream(topicPattern, new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed));\n   225→    }\n   226→\n   227→    /**\n   228→     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n   229→     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n   230→     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n   231→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   232→     * <p>\n   233→     * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\n   234→     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n   235→     * <p>\n   236→     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} using the given\n   237→     * {@code Materialized} instance.\n   238→     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n   239→     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n   240→     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n   241→     * <p>\n   242→     * You should only specify serdes in the {@link Consumed} instance as these will also be used to overwrite the\n   243→     * serdes in {@link Materialized}, i.e.,\n   244→     * <pre> {@code\n   245→     * streamBuilder.table(topic, Consumed.with(Serde.String(), Serde.String()), Materialized.<String, String, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>as(storeName))\n   246→     * }\n   247→     * </pre>\n   248→     * To query the local {@link ReadOnlyKeyValueStore} it must be obtained via\n   249→     * {@link KafkaStreams#store(StoreQueryParameters) KafkaStreams#store(...)}:\n   250→     * <pre>{@code\n   251→     * KafkaStreams streams = ...\n   252→     * StoreQueryParameters<ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>>> storeQueryParams = StoreQueryParameters.fromNameAndType(queryableStoreName, QueryableStoreTypes.timestampedKeyValueStore());\n   253→     * ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>> localStore = streams.store(storeQueryParams);\n   254→     * K key = \"some-key\";\n   255→     * ValueAndTimestamp<V> valueForKey = localStore.get(key); // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\n   256→     * }</pre>\n   257→     * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\n   258→     * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\n   259→     *\n   260→     * @param topic              the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n   261→     * @param consumed           the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters; cannot be {@code null}\n   262→     * @param materialized       the instance of {@link Materialized} used to materialize a state store; cannot be {@code null}\n   263→     * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n   264→     */\n   265→    public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic,\n   266→                                                  final Consumed<K, V> consumed,\n   267→                                                  final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\n   268→        Objects.requireNonNull(topic, \"topic can't be null\");\n   269→        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n   270→        Objects.requireNonNull(materialized, \"materialized can't be null\");\n   271→        final ConsumedInternal<K, V> consumedInternal = new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed);\n   272→        materialized.withKeySerde(consumedInternal.keySerde()).withValueSerde(consumedInternal.valueSerde());\n   273→\n   274→        final MaterializedInternal<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materializedInternal =\n   275→            new MaterializedInternal<>(materialized, internalStreamsBuilder, topic + \"-\");\n   276→\n   277→        return internalStreamsBuilder.table(topic, consumedInternal, materializedInternal);\n   278→    }\n   279→\n   280→    /**\n   281→     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n   282→     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy and default key and value deserializers as specified in the\n   283→     * {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n   284→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   285→     * <p>\n   286→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   287→     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n   288→     * <p>\n   289→     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} with an internal\n   290→     * store name. Note that store name may not be queryable through Interactive Queries.\n   313→     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n   314→     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n   315→     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n   316→     *\n   317→     * @param topic     the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n   318→     * @param consumed  the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters; cannot be {@code null}\n   319→     * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n   320→     */\n   321→    public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic,\n   322→                                                  final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n   323→        Objects.requireNonNull(topic, \"topic can't be null\");\n   324→        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n   325→        final ConsumedInternal<K, V> consumedInternal = new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed);\n   326→\n   327→        final MaterializedInternal<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materializedInternal =\n   328→            new MaterializedInternal<>(\n   329→                Materialized.with(consumedInternal.keySerde(), consumedInternal.valueSerde()),\n   330→                internalStreamsBuilder,\n   331→                topic + \"-\");\n   332→\n   333→        return internalStreamsBuilder.table(topic, consumedInternal, materializedInternal);\n   334→    }\n   335→\n   336→    /**\n   337→     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n   338→     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n   339→     * Key and value deserializers as defined by the options in {@link Materialized} are used.\n   340→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   341→     * <p>\n   342→     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n   343→     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n   344→     * <p>\n   345→     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} using the {@link Materialized} instance.\n   346→     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n   347→     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n   348→     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n   349→     *\n   350→     * @param topic         the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n   351→     * @param materialized  the instance of {@link Materialized} used to materialize a state store; cannot be {@code null}\n   352→     * @return a {@link KTable} for the specified topic\n   353→     */\n   354→    public synchronized <K, V> KTable<K, V> table(final String topic,\n   355→                                                  final Materialized<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materialized) {\n   356→        Objects.requireNonNull(topic, \"topic can't be null\");\n   357→        Objects.requireNonNull(materialized, \"materialized can't be null\");\n   358→\n   359→        final MaterializedInternal<K, V, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>> materializedInternal =\n   360→            new MaterializedInternal<>(materialized, internalStreamsBuilder, topic + \"-\");\n   361→\n   362→        final ConsumedInternal<K, V> consumedInternal =\n   363→                new ConsumedInternal<>(Consumed.with(materializedInternal.keySerde(), materializedInternal.valueSerde()));\n   364→\n   365→        return internalStreamsBuilder.table(topic, consumedInternal, materializedInternal);\n   366→    }\n   367→\n   368→    /**\n   369→     * Create a {@link GlobalKTable} for the specified topic.\n   370→     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n   371→     * <p>\n   372→     * The resulting {@link GlobalKTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} with an internal\n   373→     * store name. Note that store name may not be queryable through Interactive Queries.\n   374→     * No internal changelog topic is created since the original input topic can be used for recovery (cf.\n   375→     * methods of {@link KGroupedStream} and {@link KGroupedTable} that return a {@link KTable}).\n   376→     * <p>\n   377→     * Note that {@link GlobalKTable} always applies {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy {@code \"earliest\"}\n   378→     * regardless of the specified value in {@link StreamsConfig} or {@link Consumed}.\n   379→     * Furthermore, {@link GlobalKTable} cannot be a {@link org.apache.kafka.streams.state.VersionedBytesStoreSupplier\n   380→     * versioned state store}.\n   381→     *\n   382→     * @param topic the topic name; Creating a single {@link Processor} object\n   545→     * and returning the same object reference in {@link ProcessorSupplier#get()} is a\n   546→     * violation of the supplier pattern and leads to runtime exceptions.\n   547→     * This {@link Processor} should be used to keep the {@link StateStore} up-to-date.\n   548→     * The default {@link TimestampExtractor} as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} is used.\n   549→     * <p>\n   550→     * It is not required to connect a global store to the {@link Processor Processors},\n   551→     * or {@link org.apache.kafka.streams.kstream.KTable#transformValues(ValueTransformerWithKeySupplier, String...) java.util.Objects;\nimport java.util.Properties;\nimport java.util.regex.Pattern;\n\n/**\n * {@code StreamsBuilder} provides the high-level Kafka Streams DSL to specify a Kafka Streams topology.\n *\n * <p>\n * It is a requirement that the processing logic ({@link Topology}) be defined in a deterministic way,\n * as in, the order in which all operators are added must be predictable and the same across all application\n * instances.\n * Topologies are only identical if all operators are added in the same order.\n * If different {@link KafkaStreams} instances of the same application build different topologies the result may be\n * incompatible runtime code and unexpected results or errors\n *\n * @see Topology\n * @see KStream\n * @see KTable\n * @see GlobalKTable\n */\npublic class StreamsBuilder {\n\n    /** The actual topology that is constructed by this StreamsBuilder. */\n    protected final Topology topology;\n\n    /** The topology's internal builder. */\n    protected final InternalTopologyBuilder internalTopologyBuilder;\n\n    protected final InternalStreamsBuilder internalStreamsBuilder;\n\n    public StreamsBuilder() {\n        topology = new Topology();\n        internalTopologyBuilder = topology.internalTopologyBuilder;\n        internalStreamsBuilder = new InternalStreamsBuilder(internalTopologyBuilder, false);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@code StreamsBuilder} instance.\n     *\n     * @param topologyConfigs    the streams configs that apply at the topology level. Please refer to {@link TopologyConfig} for more detail\n     */\n    @SuppressWarnings(\"this-escape\")\n    public StreamsBuilder(final TopologyConfig topologyConfigs) {\n        topology = newTopology(topologyConfigs);\n        internalTopologyBuilder = topology.internalTopologyBuilder;\n        internalStreamsBuilder = new InternalStreamsBuilder(\n            internalTopologyBuilder,\n            TopologyConfig.InternalConfig.getBoolean(\n                topologyConfigs.originals(),\n                TopologyConfig.InternalConfig.ENABLE_PROCESS_PROCESSVALUE_FIX,\n                false\n            )\n        );\n    }\n\n    protected Topology newTopology(final TopologyConfig topologyConfigs) {\n        return new Topology(topologyConfigs);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic.\n     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, default {@link TimestampExtractor}, and default key and value\n     * deserializers as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n     * <p>\n     * If multiple topics are specified there is no ordering guarantee for records from different topics.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n     *\n     * @param topic the topic name; cannot be {@code null}\n     * @return a {@link KStream} for the specified topic\n     */\n    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final String topic) {\n        return stream(Collections.singleton(topic));\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic.\n     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n     *\n     * @param topic the topic names; must contain at least one topic name\n     * @return a {@link KStream} for the specified topics\n     */\n    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Collection<String> topics) {\n        return stream(topics, Consumed.with(null, null));\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topics.\n     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n     * <p>\n     * If multiple topics are specified there is no ordering guarantee for records from different topics.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n     *\n     * @param topics the topic names; must contain at least one topic name\n     * @param consumed      the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters\n     * @return a {@link KStream} for the specified topics\n     */\n    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Collection<String> topics,\n                                                    final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n        Objects.requireNonNull(topics, \"topics can't be null\");\n        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n        return internalStreamsBuilder.stream(topics, new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed));\n    }\n\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n     * The default {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, default {@link TimestampExtractor}, and default key and value\n     * deserializers as specified in the {@link StreamsConfig config} are used.\n     * <p>\n     * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n     * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. This also means that the work\n     * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n     * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n     *\n     * @param topicPattern the pattern to match for topic names\n     * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n     */\n    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern) {\n        return stream(topicPattern, Consumed.with(null, null));\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KStream} from the specified topic pattern.\n     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n     * <p>\n     * If multiple topics are matched by the specified pattern, the created {@link KStream} will read data from all of\n     * them and there is no ordering guarantee between records from different topics. This also means that the work\n     * will not be parallelized for multiple topics, and the number of tasks will scale with the maximum partition\n     * count of any matching topic rather than the total number of partitions across all topics.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topics must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case it is the user's responsibility to repartition the data before any key based operation\n     * (like aggregation or join) is applied to the returned {@link KStream}.\n     *\n     * @param topicPattern  the pattern to match for topic names\n     * @param consumed      the instance of {@link Consumed} used to define optional parameters\n     * @return a {@link KStream} for topics matching the regex pattern.\n     */\n    public synchronized <K, V> KStream<K, V> stream(final Pattern topicPattern,\n                                                    final Consumed<K, V> consumed) {\n        Objects.requireNonNull(topicPattern, \"topicPattern can't be null\");\n        Objects.requireNonNull(consumed, \"consumed can't be null\");\n        return internalStreamsBuilder.stream(topicPattern, new ConsumedInternal<>(consumed));\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Create a {@link KTable} for the specified topic.\n     * The {@code \"auto.offset.reset\"} strategy, {@link TimestampExtractor}, key and value deserializers\n     * are defined by the options in {@link Consumed} are used.\n     * Input {@link KeyValue records} with {@code null} key will be dropped.\n     * <p>\n     * Note that the specified input topic must be partitioned by key.\n     * If this is not the case the returned {@link KTable} will be corrupted.\n     * <p>\n     * The resulting {@link KTable} will be materialized in a local {@link KeyValueStore} using the given\n     * {@code Materialized} instance.\n     * An internal changelog topic is created by default. Because the source topic can\n     * be used for recovery, you can avoid creating the changelog topic by setting\n     * the {@code \"topology.optimization\"} to {@code \"all\"} in the {@link StreamsConfig}.\n     * <p>\n     * You should only specify serdes in the {@link Consumed} instance as these will also be used to overwrite the\n     * serdes in {@link Materialized}, i.e.,\n     * <pre> {@code\n     * streamBuilder.table(topic, Consumed.with(Serde.String(), Serde.String()), Materialized.<String, String, KeyValueStore<Bytes, byte[]>as(storeName))\n     * }\n     * </pre>\n     * To query the local {@link ReadOnlyKeyValueStore} it must be obtained via\n     * {@link KafkaStreams#store(StoreQueryParameters) KafkaStreams#store(...)}:\n     * <pre>{@code\n     * KafkaStreams streams = ...\n     * StoreQueryParameters<ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>>> storeQueryParams = StoreQueryParameters.fromNameAndType(queryableStoreName, QueryableStoreTypes.timestampedKeyValueStore());\n     * ReadOnlyKeyValueStore<K, ValueAndTimestamp<V>> localStore = streams.store(storeQueryParams);\n     * K key = \"some-key\";\n     * ValueAndTimestamp<V> valueForKey = localStore.get(key); // key must be local (application state is shared over all running Kafka Streams instances)\n     * }</pre>\n     * For non-local keys, a custom RPC mechanism must be implemented using {@link KafkaStreams#metadataForAllStreamsClients()} to\n     * query the value of the key on a parallel running instance of your Kafka Streams application.\n     *\n     * @param topic              the topic name;
